						<div id="siteNotice"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>
						<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">Automotive industry</span></h1>
			<div id="bodyContent">
								<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-navigation">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><p>The <b>automotive industry</b> is a term that covers a wide range of companies and organisations involved in the design, development, manufacture, marketing, and selling of <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">motor vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trailer_(vehicle)" title="Trailer (vehicle)">towed vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle" title="Motorcycle">motorcycles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moped" title="Moped">mopeds</a>. It is one of the world's most important <a href="/wiki/Economic_sector" title="Economic sector">economic sectors</a> by <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a>.</p>
<p>The term <i>automotive industry</i> usually does not include industries dedicated to the maintenance of automobiles following delivery to the end-user, such as <a href="/wiki/Automobile_repair_shop" title="Automobile repair shop">repair shops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motor_fuel" title="Motor fuel">motor fuel</a> <a href="/wiki/Filling_stations" title="Filling stations" class="mw-redirect">filling stations</a>.</p>
<p>The term <i>automotive</i> was created from Greek <i>autos</i> (self), and Latin <i>motivus</i> (of motion) to represent any form of self-powered vehicle. This term was proposed by <a href="/wiki/SAE_International" title="SAE International">SAE</a> member <a href="/wiki/Elmer_Sperry" title="Elmer Sperry" class="mw-redirect">Elmer Sperry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-STS_of_US_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STS_of_US-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_automobile" title="History of the automobile">History of the automobile</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg/250px-Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg" width="250" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg/375px-Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg/500px-Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_B_Jeffery_Works_Drawing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Thomas_B._Jeffery_Company" title="Thomas B. Jeffery Company">Thomas B. Jeffery</a> automobile factory in Kenosha, Wisconsin, c.1916</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg/250px-Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg" width="250" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg/375px-Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg/500px-Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg 2x" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chaine_Citroen_typea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf13/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn" title="Citroën">Citroën</a> assembly line in 1918</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The automotive industry began in the 1890s with hundreds of manufacturers that pioneered the <a href="/wiki/Brass_Era_car" title="Brass Era car">horseless carriage</a>. For many decades, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> led the world in total automobile production. In 1929 before the Great Depression, the world had 32,028,500 automobiles in use, and the U.S. automobile industry produced over 90% of them. At that time the U.S. had one car per 4.87 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the U.S. produced about 75 percent of world's auto production. In 1980, the U.S. was overtaken by Japan and became world's leader again in 1994. In 2006, Japan narrowly passed the U.S. in production and held this rank until 2009, when China took the top spot with 13.8 million units. By producing 19.2 million units in 2012, China produced almost than twice the number of automobiles made in the U.S. second place with 10.3 million units, while Japan was in third place with 9.9 million units.<sup id="cite_ref-Production_Statistics_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Statistics-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Safety">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Safety" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety" title="Automobile safety">Automobile safety</a></div>
<p>Safety is a state that implies to be protected from any risk, danger, damage or cause of injury. In the automotive industry, safety means that users, operators or <a href="/wiki/Manufacturers" title="Manufacturers" class="mw-redirect">manufacturers</a> do not face any risk or danger coming from the motor vehicle or its spare parts. Safety for the automotives themselves implies that there is no risk of damage.</p>
<p>Safety in the automotive industry is particularly important and therefore highly regulated. <a href="/wiki/Automobiles" title="Automobiles" class="mw-redirect">Automobiles</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicles" title="Motor vehicles" class="mw-redirect">motor vehicles</a> have to comply with a certain number of norms and regulations, whether local or international, in order to be accepted on the market. The standard <a href="/wiki/ISO_26262" title="ISO 26262">ISO 26262</a> <sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> (_See also main article:_ <a href="/wiki/ISO_26262" title="ISO 26262">ISO 26262</a>) for instance is considered as one of the best practice framework for achieving automotive <a href="/wiki/Functional_safety" title="Functional safety" class="mw-redirect">functional safety</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> That is, to ensure that motored vehicles meet all requirements for safe manufacturing and operation for end-users.</p>
<p>In case of safety issues, danger, product defect or faulty procedure during the manufacturing of the motor vehicle, the maker can request to return either a batch or the entire production run. This procedure is called <a href="/wiki/Product_recall" title="Product recall">product recall</a>. Product recalls happen in every industry and can be production-related or stem from the raw material.</p>
<p>Product and operation tests and inspections at different stages of the <a href="/wiki/Value_chain" title="Value chain">value chain</a> are made to avoid these product recalls by ensuring end-user security and safety and compliance with the automotive industry requirements. However, the automotive industry is still particularly concerned about product recalls,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> which cause considerable financial consequences.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economy">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Economy" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_by_country" title="Automotive industry by country">Automotive industry by country</a></div>
<p>Around the world, there were about 806 million cars and light trucks on the road in 2007, consuming over 260 billion US gallons (980,000,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of gasoline and diesel fuel yearly.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The automobile is a primary mode of transportation for many developed economies. The Detroit branch of <a href="/wiki/Boston_Consulting_Group" title="Boston Consulting Group">Boston Consulting Group</a> predicts that, by 2014, one-third of world demand will be in the four <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC</a> markets (Brazil, Russia, India and China). Other potentially powerful automotive markets are <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Emerging auto markets already buy more cars than established markets. According to a J.D. Power study, emerging markets accounted for 51 percent of the global <a href="/wiki/Light_commercial_vehicle" title="Light commercial vehicle">light-vehicle</a> sales in 2010. The study expects this trend to accelerate.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_motor_vehicle_production">World motor vehicle production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: World motor vehicle production">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: World motor vehicle production" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_motor_vehicle_production" title="List of countries by motor vehicle production">List of countries by motor vehicle production</a></div>
<p>For many decades, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> led the world in total automobile production. In 1929 before the Great Depression, the world had 32,028,500 automobiles in use, and the US automobile industry produced over 90% of them. At that time the U.S. had one car per 4.87 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> After WWII the U.S. issued 3/4 of world's auto production. In 1980 the U.S. was overtaken by Japan and became world's leader again in 1994. In 2006, Japan narrowly passed the U.S. in production and held this rank until 2009, when China took the top spot with 13.8 million units. By producing 18.4 million units in 2011, China produced more than twice the number of automobiles made by the U.S. in second place with 8.7 million units, while Japan was in third place with 8.4 million units.<sup id="cite_ref-Production_Statistics_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Statistics-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_year">By year</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: By year">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: By year" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><big><b>Global production of motorvehicles</b></big></p>
<p>(cars and commercial vehicles)</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr style="background-color:#C0C0C0;font-weight:bold" align="center" valign="bottom">
<td width="48" height="13">Year</td>
<td width="67">Production</td>
<td width="52">Change</td>
<td width="70">Source</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td height="13" align="center" valign="bottom">1997</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_relationships">Company relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Company relationships">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Company relationships" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>It is common for automobile manufacturers to hold stakes in other automobile manufacturers. These ownerships can be explored under the detail for the individual companies.</p>
<p>Notable current relationships include:<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a> holds a 20% stake in <a href="/wiki/Eicher_Motors" title="Eicher Motors">Eicher Motors</a>, a 10.0% stake in <a href="/wiki/KAMAZ" title="KAMAZ" class="mw-redirect">KAMAZ</a>, a 4.7% stake in <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>, a 6.75% stake in <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> and a 3.1% in the <a href="/wiki/Renault-Nissan_Alliance" title="Renault-Nissan Alliance" class="mw-redirect">Renault-Nissan Alliance</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dongfeng_Motor_Corporation" title="Dongfeng Motor Corporation" class="mw-redirect">Dongfeng Motor Corporation</a> is involved in joint ventures with several companies around the world, including: <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> (Japan), <a href="/wiki/Hyundai" title="Hyundai">Hyundai</a> (South Korea), <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motors" title="Nissan Motors" class="mw-redirect">Nissan</a> (Japan), <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Diesel" title="Nissan Diesel" class="mw-redirect">Nissan Diesel</a> (Sweden), and <a href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citroen" title="PSA Peugeot Citroen" class="mw-redirect">PSA Peugeot Citroen</a> (France).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> holds a 90% stake in <a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferrari</a> and a 61.8% stake in <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a> holds a 3% stake in <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> and a 12.1% share in <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Geely_Automobile" title="Geely Automobile" class="mw-redirect">Geely Automobile</a> holds a 23% stake in <a href="/wiki/Manganese_Bronze_Holdings" title="Manganese Bronze Holdings">Manganese Bronze Holdings</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> holds a 7% stake in <a href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citroen" title="PSA Peugeot Citroen" class="mw-redirect">PSA Peugeot Citroen</a>, General Motors and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Automotive_Industry_Corporation" title="Shanghai Automotive Industry Corporation" class="mw-redirect">Shanghai Automotive Industry Corporation</a> (SAIC), and has two joint ventures in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_GM" title="Shanghai GM">Shanghai General Motors</a> and <a href="/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile" class="mw-redirect">SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile</a>. Both also hold an equal 50% stake in <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_India_Private_Limited" title="General Motors India Private Limited">General Motors India Private Limited</a>. And General Motors holds a 94% stake in <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Automotive_Industry_Corporation" title="Shanghai Automotive Industry Corporation" class="mw-redirect">SAIC Group</a> holds a 6% stake.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mahindra_%26_Mahindra" title="Mahindra &amp; Mahindra">Mahindra &amp; Mahindra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Navistar_International" title="Navistar International">Navistar International</a> has a joint venture called <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_Navistar" title="Mahindra Navistar">Mahindra Trucks and Buses Limited</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_%26_Mahindra" title="Mahindra &amp; Mahindra">Mahindra &amp; Mahindra</a> owns 51% and <a href="/wiki/Navistar_International" title="Navistar International">Navistar International</a> owns 49%.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN SE</a> holds a 17.01% voting stake in <a href="/wiki/Scania_(company)" title="Scania (company)" class="mw-redirect">Scania</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche Automobil Holding SE</a> has a 50.74% voting stake in <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>. The Porsche automotive business is fully owned by the Volkswagen Group.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Motors" title="Nissan Motors" class="mw-redirect">Nissan Motors</a> have an alliance( <a href="/wiki/Renault-Nissan_Alliance" title="Renault-Nissan Alliance" class="mw-redirect">Renault-Nissan Alliance</a> ) involving two global companies linked by cross-shareholding, with Renault holding 44.3% of Nissan shares, and Nissan holding 15% of (non-voting) Renault shares. The alliance holds a 3.1% share in <a href="/wiki/Daimler_AG" title="Daimler AG">Daimler AG</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> holds a 25% stake in <a href="/wiki/AvtoVAZ" title="AvtoVAZ">AvtoVAZ</a> and a 80.1% stake in <a href="/wiki/Renault_Samsung" title="Renault Samsung" class="mw-redirect">Renault Samsung</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> holds a 51% stake in <a href="/wiki/Daihatsu" title="Daihatsu">Daihatsu</a>, 16.5% in <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Heavy_Industries" title="Fuji Heavy Industries">Fuji Heavy Industries</a>, parent company of <a href="/wiki/Subaru" title="Subaru">Subaru</a>, and a 10% stake in <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a> holds a 37.73% stake in <a href="/wiki/Scania_(company)" title="Scania (company)" class="mw-redirect">Scania</a> (68.6% voting rights), and a 53.7% stake in <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN SE</a> (55.9% voting rights). Volkswagen is integrating Scania, MAN and its own truck division into one division.<a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a> has a 19.9% stake in <a href="/wiki/Suzuki" title="Suzuki">Suzuki</a>, and Suzuki has a 5% stake in Volkswagen.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PACCAR" title="PACCAR" class="mw-redirect">Paccar inc.</a> has a 19% stake in <a href="/wiki/Tatra_(company)" title="Tatra (company)">Tatra</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> also formed a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> and gained access to Fiat’s diesel engine technology.<a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> sells <a href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> cars in India through a 50/50 joint venture Fiat Automobiles India Limited, and is looking to extend its relationship with Fiat and <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a> to other segments</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Top_vehicle_manufacturing_groups_by_volume">Top vehicle manufacturing groups by volume</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Top vehicle manufacturing groups by volume">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Top vehicle manufacturing groups by volume" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The table below shows the world's largest motor vehicle manufacturing groups, along with the <a href="/wiki/Marque" title="Marque" class="mw-redirect">marques</a> produced by each one. The table is ranked by 2011 <i>end of year</i> production figures from the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_of_Motor_Vehicle_Manufacturers" title="International Organization of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers" class="mw-redirect">International Organization of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers</a> (OICA)<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> for the parent group, and then alphabetically by marque. Joint ventures are not reflected in this table. Production figures of joint ventures are typically included in OICA rankings, which can become a source of controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><b>Note:</b> This section does not include the selling of other products in a region example; <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">CAT</a> sells commercial vehicles in the US, Canada, Mexico, and Australia, and New Zealand. But sells its other products worldwide. If the table(markets) says that a brand is available in example North America, it doesn't include Territories controlled by countries on other continents. Example; GMC isn't available in any European territories within North America.</p>

<th>Markets</th>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="By_total_production">By total production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: By total production">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: By total production" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Quantifying the total production of a manufacturer, from their start-up, is a difficult task, because of frequent company ownership changes. However some producers, and independent sources, provide some valuable statistics:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> reached 200 000 000 vehicles as of July 2012 (after 77 years of production).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_automotive_manufacturers">Minor automotive manufacturers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Minor automotive manufacturers">edit source</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Minor automotive manufacturers" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minor_automotive_manufacturing_groups" title="Minor automotive manufacturing groups">Minor automotive manufacturing groups</a></div>
<p>There are many automobile manufacturers other than the major global companies. They are mostly regional or operating in niche markets.</p>
